<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.mccormick.2018.714">McCormick et al [2018]</a>
</p></div></dd><dt>2. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.4.2"><p class="no_margin">Despite the related genes and manifestations of hemiplegia and seizure, <i>ATP1A2</i> is expressed mainly in astrocytes instead of neurons [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.mcgrail.1991.381">McGrail et al 1991</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sweadner.2019.e303">Sweadner et al 2019</a>], and the underlying pathophysiology is likely to be different from that of <i>ATP1A3</i>-related disorder [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.swoboda.2004.884">Swoboda et al 2004</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.jen.2007.523">Jen et al 2007</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sweadner.2019.e303">Sweadner et al 2019</a>].</p></div></dd><dt>3. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.4.3"><p class="no_margin">
<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.hashimoto.2022.3374">Hashimoto et al [2022]</a>
</p></div></dd><dt>4. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.4.4"><p class="no_margin">
<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.panagiotakaki.2024.224">Panagiotakaki et al [2024]</a>
</p></div></dd><dt>5. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.4.5"><p class="no_margin">
<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sen.2019.122">Sen et al [2019]</a>
</p></div></dd><dt>6. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.4.6"><p class="no_margin">
<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.cordani.2022.69">Cordani et al [2022]</a>
</p></div></dd></dl></div></div></div></div><div id="rapid-odp.CAPOS_Syndrome_1"><h3>CAPOS Syndrome</h3><p>The combination of cerebellar ataxia, areflexia, pes cavus, optic atrophy, and sensorineural hearing loss is unique to CAPOS syndrome. However, an individual with the CAPOS syndrome-related <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> p.Glu818Lys may present with a subset of these features (e.g., sensorineural hearing loss in association with areflexia; or cerebellar ataxia, areflexia, optic atrophy, and sensorineural hearing without pes cavus) or may present with a single feature (e.g., apparently <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/isolated/">isolated</a> hearing loss [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.lee.2020.5768">Lee et al 2020</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.lax.2021.120003">Lax et al 2021</a>]). (Note: Individuals with the p.Glu818Lys pathogenic variant and only a single feature, or a subset of CAPOS syndrome-related features, should be considered at risk for progression.) Subsets of features seen in CAPOS syndrome and the individual features themselves elicit a broad differential diagnosis including mitochondrial and peroxisomal disorders.</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.RECAFIPWE_1"><h3>RECA/FIPWE</h3><p>The differential diagnosis of fever-induced manifestations such as weakness and ataxia is broad and includes the episodic ataxias (see <a href="/books/n/gene/ataxias/">Hereditary Ataxia Overview</a>) [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.olszewska.2023.3377">Olszewska et al 2023</a>] and numerous other genetic and non-genetic causes of ataxia. Acute infection and autoimmune disease in particular must be excluded from the differential diagnosis of relapsing encephalopathy with cerebellar ataxia (RECA)&#x000a0;/ fever-induced paroxysmal weakness and encephalopathy (FIPWE).</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.RapidOnset_DystoniaParkinsonis"><h3>Rapid-Onset Dystonia-Parkinsonism</h3><p>Forms of dystonia-parkinsonism that are more common than rapid-onset dystonia-parkinsonism (RDP) (see <a href="/books/n/gene/dystonia-ov/">Hereditary Dystonia Overview</a> and <a href="/books/n/gene/parkinson-overview/">Parkinson Disease Overview</a>) and potentially treatable must be excluded from the differential diagnosis. Evaluations should include brain MRI and assessment for <a href="/books/n/gene/wilson/">Wilson disease</a>. Additionally, administration of levodopa should be trialed; in RDP, the brain MRI is grossly normal and the response to levodopa is usually transient or minimal, with only one reported exception [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.termsarasab.2015.336">Termsarasab et al 2015</a>].</p><p>The differential diagnosis of RDP includes the genes listed in <a href="/books/NBK1115/table/rapid-odp.T.selected_genes_of_interest_i_1/?report=objectonly" target="object" rid-ob="figobrapidodpTselectedgenesofinteresti1">Table 5</a>.</p><div id="rapid-odp.T.selected_genes_of_interest_i_1" class="table"><h3><span class="label">Table 5. </span></h3><div class="caption"><p>Selected Genes of Interest in the Differential Diagnosis of Rapid-Onset Dystonia-Parkinsonism</p></div><p class="large-table-link" style="display:none"><span class="right"><a href="/books/NBK1115/table/rapid-odp.T.selected_genes_of_interest_i_1/?report=objectonly" target="object">View in own window</a></span></p><div class="large_tbl" </td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.selected_genes_of_interest_i_1_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"><a href="/books/n/gene/pink1-pd/"><i>PINK1</i> type of young-onset Parkinson disease</a> (PARK-<i>PINK1</i>)</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.selected_genes_of_interest_i_1_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">AR</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.selected_genes_of_interest_i_1_1_1_1_4" rowspan="2" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Persons w/young-onset parkinsonism may have limb dystonia as an early manifestation; however, unlike persons w/RDP, they should have a significant &#x00026; sustained response to levodopa.</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.selected_genes_of_interest_i_1_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<i>PRKN</i>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.selected_genes_of_interest_i_1_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"><a href="/books/n/gene/jpd/">Parkin type of early-onset Parkinson disease</a> (PARK-<i>Parkin</i>)</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.selected_genes_of_interest_i_1_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">AR</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><div><dl class="temp-labeled-list small"><dt></dt><dd><div><p class="no_margin">AD = <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a>; AR = <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-recessive/">autosomal recessive</a>; DYT = dystonia; MOI = <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/mode-of-inheritance/">mode of inheritance</a>; PARK = parkinsonism; RDP = rapid-onset dystonia-parkinsonism</p></div></dd><dt>1. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.5.1"><p class="no_margin"><a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.bressman.2002.1780">Bressman et al [2002]</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.kabakci.2005.860">Kabakci et al [2005]</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.geyer.2006.780">Geyer &#x00026; Bressman [2006]</a></p></div></dd><dt>2. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.5.2"><p class="no_margin">
<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.termsarasab.2015.336">Termsarasab et al [2015]</a>
</p></div></dd></dl></div></div></div></div></div><div id="rapid-odp.Management"><h2 id="_rapid-odp_Management_">Management</h2><p>No clinical practice guidelines for <i>ATP1A3-</i>related disorder have been published. In the absence of established clinical practice guidelines, the authors offer the recommendations discussed in this section based on their collective experience in working with more than 20 families over more than 15 years.</p><div id="rapid-odp.Evaluations_Following_Initial"><h3>Evaluations Following Initial Diagnosis</h3><p>To establish the extent of disease and needs in an individual diagnosed with <i>ATP1A3</i>-related disorder, the evaluations summarized in <a href="/books/NBK1115/table/rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom/?report=objectonly" target="object" rid-ob="figobrapidodpTatp1a3relateddisorderrecom">Table 6</a> (if not performed as part of the evaluation that led to diagnosis) are recommended.</p><div id="rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom" class="table"><h3><span class="label">Table 6. </span></h3><div class="caption"><p><i>ATP1A3-</i>Related Disorder: Recommended Evaluations Following Initial Diagnosis</p></div><p class="large-table-link" style="display:none"><span class="right"><a href="/books/NBK1115/table/rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom/?report=objectonly" target="object">View in own window</a></span></p><div class="large_tbl" id="__rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_lrgtbl__"><table class="no_bottom_margin"><thead><tr><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">System/Concern</th><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">Evaluation</th><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">Comment</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Neurologic</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Neurologic eval by neurologist experienced in movement disorders</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">Assess for:
<ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Episodic or persistent weakness;</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Movement disorders (e.g., dystonia, chorea, ataxia);</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Dysfunctions of speech &#x00026; swallowing;</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Hypo- or hypertonia;</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Cognitive manifestations (e.g., apraxia, frontal lobe dysfunction).</div></li></ul>
Obtain history of:
<ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Seizures;</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Headaches.</div></li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Musculoskeletal/ADL</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Orthopedics&#x000a0;/ physical medicine &#x00026; rehab&#x000a0;/ PT &#x00026; OT eval</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Assess for:
<ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Gross motor &#x00026; fine motor skills;</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Contractures, pes cavus, kyphoscoliosis;</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Mobility, ADL, need for adaptive devices;</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Need for PT (to improve gross motor skills) &#x00026;/or OT (to improve fine motor skills).</div></li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Speech</b>

<br />
<b>Psychiatric</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Developmental pediatrician</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Younger children: to incl screening for sleep disturbances, ADHD, anxiety, &#x00026;/or findings suggestive of ASD</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Neuropsychologist</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Older children &#x00026; adults:
<ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>To assess for mood disorder (depression, anxiety, psychosis, OCD)</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>To assess for cognitive dysfunction, particularly language (esp fluency), executive function</div></li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Ophthalmologic involvement</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Ophthalmologic eval</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Assess for abnormal ocular movement, best corrected visual acuity, refractive errors, strabismus, &#x00026; more complex findings (e.g., optic atrophy) that may require referral for subspecialty care &#x00026;/or low vision services.</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Audiologic eval</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Evaluate for sensorineural hearing loss.</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">EKG &#x00026; echocardiogram</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Evaluate for cardiac conduction abnormalities.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Consider referral to cardiologist.</div></li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Genetic counseling</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">By genetics professionals&#x000a0;<sup>2</sup></td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Obtain a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pedigree/">pedigree</a> &#x00026; inform affected persons &#x00026; their families re nature, MOI, &#x00026; implications of <i>ATP1A3</i>-related disorder to facilitate medical &#x00026; personal decision making</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Family support</b>
<br />
<b>&#x00026; resources</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">By clinicians, wider care team, &#x00026; family support organizations</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Assessment of family &#x00026; social structure to determine need for:
<ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Community or <a href="#rapid-odp.Resources">online resources</a> such as <a href="https://www.p2pusa.org/" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">Parent to Parent</a></div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Social work involvement for parental support</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Home nursing referral</div></li></ul>
</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><div><dl class="temp-labeled-list small"><dt></dt><dd><div><p class="no_margin">ADHD = attention-deficit/hyperactivity disorder; ADL = activities of daily living; ASD = autism spectrum disorder; IEP= individualized education plan; MOI = <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/mode-of-inheritance/">mode of inheritance</a>; OCD = obsessive-compulsive disorder; OT = occupational therapy; PT = physical therapy</p></div></dd><dt>1. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.6.1"><p class="no_margin">In the US, a 504 plan involves legally required classroom accommodations or modifications (e.g., front-of-class seating, assistive technology devices, modified assignments).</p></div></dd><dt>2. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.6.2"><p class="no_margin">Clinical geneticist, certified genetic counselor, certified genetic nurse, genetics advanced practice provider (nurse practitioner or physician assistant)</p></div></dd></dl></div></div></div></div><div id="rapid-odp.Treatment_of_Manifestations"><h3>Treatment of Manifestations</h3><p>There is no cure for <i>ATP1A3-</i>related disorder. Supportive care to improve quality of life, maximize function, and reduce complications is recommended. This ideally involves multidisciplinary care by specialists in relevant fields (see <a href="/books/NBK1115/table/rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat/?report=objectonly" target="object" rid-ob="figobrapidodpTatp1a3relateddisordertreat">Table 7</a>.</p><div id="rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat" class="table"><h3><span class="label">Table 7. </span></h3><div class="caption"><p><i>ATP1A3-</i>Related Disorder: Treatment of Manifestations</p></div><p class="large-table-link" style="display:none"><span class="right"><a href="/books/NBK1115/table/rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat/?report=objectonly" target="object">View in own window</a></span></p><div class="large_tbl" id="__rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_lrgtbl__"><table class="no_bottom_margin"><thead><tr><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_1" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">Manifestation/Concern</th><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Treatment</th><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">Considerations/Other</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_1" rowspan="3" scope="rowgroup" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Hemiplegic events</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Flunarizine (in persons w/AHC) is used prophylactically to &#x02193; frequency &#x00026; severity of events.&#x000a0;<sup>1,&#x000a0;2</sup></td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Some studies have suggested that flunarizine may be particularly efficacious in persons w/p.Glu815Lys variant.&#x000a0;<sup>3</sup></div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Abrupt withdrawal of flunarizine has been assoc w/deterioration in clinical status.&#x000a0;<sup>4</sup></div></li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="col" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Topiramate&#x000a0;<sup>5</sup> (in persons w/AHC)</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"></td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Ketogenic diet (in persons w/AHC)</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">3 persons responded to ketogenic diet.&#x000a0;<sup>6</sup></td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Dystonia</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Anticholinergics (trihexyphenidyl), botulinum toxin injections, benzodiazepines, dopamine agonists, or levodopa may provide symptomatic relief.&#x000a0;<sup>1</sup></td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>In RDP, there is no known way to prevent abrupt onset of dystonia.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Caution is advised re side effects of sedation &#x00026; mood/impulsivity as for persons w/movement disorders in general.</div></li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_1" rowspan="4" scope="rowgroup" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Acute spasms or attacks</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Chloral hydrate, melatonin, or other sleep-inducing medication (in persons w/AHC)</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">For recurrent brief or more prolonged tonic or dystonic episodes assoc w/alterations in consciousness; low threshold for suspicion of seizure activity</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Benzodiazepines are used as rescue drugs in persons w/AHC.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Trial high-dose benzodiazepines in persons w/RDP.</div></li></ul>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">No systematic study of benzodiazepine therapy has been published.</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Sleep (in persons w/AHC)</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;"><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Adult: place in quiet, dark room.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Child: put down for a nap.</div></li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Avoidance of triggers</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">See <a href="#rapid-odp.AgentsCircumstances_to_Avoid">Agents/Circumstances to Avoid</a>.</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Seizures</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Standard treatment w/ASM by experienced neurologist</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Strongly recommend developing seizure care plan w/provision of rescue therapy for prolonged seizures (if indicated).</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_treat_1_1_1_1" scope="row" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

anti-seizure medication; OT = occupational therapy/therapist; PT = physical therapy/therapist</p></div></dd><dt>1. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.7.1"><p class="no_margin">Pallidal deep brain stimulation has not been effective [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.deutschl_nder.2005.254">Deutschl&#x000e4;nder et al 2005</a>; <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.kamm.2008.1501">Kamm et al 2008</a>; <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.br_cke.2014.76">Br&#x000fc;cke et al 2014</a>; A Brashear, personal communication].</p></div></dd><dt>2. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.7.2"><p class="no_margin">Flunarizine has remained the most prescribed therapy for prophylaxis of episodic neurologic dysfunction in AHC for more than two decades.</p></div></dd><dt>3. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.7.3"><p class="no_margin"><a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sasaki.2014a.153">Sasaki et al [2014a]</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.cordani.2021.658451">Cordani et al et al [2012]</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.yang.2014.e97274">Yang et al [2014]</a></p></div></dd><dt>6. </dt><dd><div id="rapid-odp.TF.7.6"><p class="no_margin"><a class="bk_pop" </td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Visual acuity</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Per treating ophthalmologist(s)</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_2" colspan="1" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Low vision services</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Per treating clinicians</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_1" colspan="2" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Cardiovascular</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Per treating cardiologist</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Per treating cardiologist</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_1" rowspan="2" scope="rowgroup" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Sensorineural hearing loss (SNHL)</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_1" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Persons known to have SNHL</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Per treating audiologist</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Per treating audiologist</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_1" colspan="1" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Persons at risk for SNHL</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Screening audiogram</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">At initial eval; then 1x or 2x/yr or as needed</td></tr><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_1" colspan="2" scope="row" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">
<b>Family/Community</b>
</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_2" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Assess family need for social work support (e.g., palliative/respite care, home nursing, other local resources), care coordination, or follow-up <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/genetic-counseling/">genetic counseling</a> if new questions arise (e.g., family planning).</td><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom_1_1_1_1_3" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">At each visit</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><div><dl class="temp-labeled-list small"><dt></dt><dd><div><p class="no_margin">ADL = activities of daily living</p></div></dd></dl></div></div></div></div><div id="rapid-odp.AgentsCircumstances_to_Avoid"><h3>Agents/Circumstances to Avoid</h3><p>To the extent possible, individuals who are <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/heterozygous/">heterozygous</a> for an <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> should avoid agents/circumstances known to trigger onset of <i>ATP1A3-</i>related disorder manifestations and/or episodes [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sweney.2009.e534">Sweney et al 2009</a>], including the following:</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Physical, psychological (e.g., missed meals, sleep deprivation), and emotional stress (e.g., excitement, fear)</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Environmental stress (e.g., bright sunlight or fluorescent lighting, heat/cold, excessive noise, crowds)</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Excessive or atypically strenuous exercise (e.g., walking farther than usual)</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Alcohol binges</div></li></ul><p>Illness, infections, and fever are common triggers. While practical preventive strategies are lacking, unnecessary exposure should be avoided.</p><p>Helmets and protective devices to prevent head injuries should be worn when participating in activities with risk of fall.</p><p>There is no known reason to avoid vaccinations.</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.Evaluation_of_Relatives_at_Ris"><h3>Evaluation of Relatives at Risk</h3><p>It is appropriate to clarify the genetic status of apparently asymptomatic older and younger at-risk relatives of an individual with <i>ATP1A3</i>-related disorder in order to identify as early as possible those who should be evaluated for cardiac conduction abnormalities (see <a href="/books/NBK1115/table/rapid-odp.T.atp1a3related_disorder_recom/?report=objectonly" target="object" rid-ob="figobrapidodpTatp1a3relateddisorderrecom">Table 6</a>) and who should avoid triggers such as excessive alcohol and exercise (see <a href="#rapid-odp.AgentsCircumstances_to_Avoid">Agents/Circumstances to Avoid</a>).</p><p>See <a href="#rapid-odp.Related_Genetic_Counseling_Iss">Genetic Counseling</a> for issues related to testing of at-risk relatives for <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/genetic-counseling/">genetic counseling</a> purposes.</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.Pregnancy_Management"><h3>Pregnancy Management</h3><p>It is recommended that during pregnancy a woman with <i>ATP1A3</i>-related disorder be monitored for manifestations of RDP, onset of which has followed childbirth in some (not all) women who are <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/heterozygous/">heterozygous</a> for an <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>. Pregnancy can also trigger worsening of symptoms in women with CAPOS syndrome [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.chang.2018.235">Chang et al 2018</a>].</p><p>In principle, abortion or cesarean section could be sufficiently stressful to trigger an episode.</p><p>In general, women with epilepsy or a seizure disorder from any cause are at greater risk for mortality during pregnancy than pregnant women without a seizure disorder; use of anti-seizure medication (ASM) during pregnancy reduces this risk. However, exposure to ASMs may increase the risk for adverse fetal outcome (depending on the drug used, the dose, and the stage of pregnancy at which medication is taken). Nevertheless, the risk of an adverse outcome to the fetus from ASM exposure is often less than that associated with exposure to an untreated maternal seizure disorder. Use of ASMs to treat a maternal seizure disorder during pregnancy is typically recommended. Discussion of the risks and benefits of using a given ASM during pregnancy should ideally take place before conception. Transitioning to a lower-risk ASM before pregnancy may be possible [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sarma.2016.467">Sarma et al 2016</a>].</p><p>See <a href="https://www.mothertobaby.org/" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">MotherToBaby</a> for further information on medication use during pregnancy.</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.Therapies_Under_Investigation"><h3>Therapies Under Investigation</h3><p>A clinical trial studying the variable phenotypic presentations of <i>ATP1A3</i>-related disorder is recruiting (<a href="https://www.clinicaltrials.gov/study/NCT00682513" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">NCT00682513</a>).</p><p>Search <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">ClinicalTrials.gov</a> in the US and <a href="https://www.clinicaltrialsregister.eu/ctr-search/search" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">EU Clinical Trials Register</a> in Europe for information on clinical studies for a wide range of diseases and conditions.</p></div></div><div id="rapid-odp.Genetic_Counseling"><h2 id="_rapid-odp_Genetic_Counseling_">Genetic Counseling</h2><p>
<i>Genetic counseling is the process of providing individuals and families with
information on the nature, mode(s) of inheritance, and implications of genetic disorders to help them
make informed medical and personal decisions. The following section deals with genetic
risk assessment and the use of family history and genetic testing to clarify genetic
status for family members; it is not meant to address all personal, cultural, or
ethical issues that may arise or to substitute for consultation with a genetics
professional</i>. &#x02014;ED.</p><div id="rapid-odp.Mode_of_Inheritance"><h3>Mode of Inheritance</h3><p><i>ATP1A3</i>-related disorder &#x02013; including the four historically defined phenotypes of alternating hemiplegia of childhood (AHC); cerebellar ataxia, areflexia, pes cavus, optic atrophy, sensorineural hearing loss (CAPOS) syndrome; relapsing encephalopathy with cerebellar ataxia (RECA)&#x000a0;/ fever-induced paroxysmal weakness and encephalopathy (FIPWE); and rapid-onset dystonia-parkinsonism (RDP) &#x02013; is inherited in an <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/autosomal-dominant/">autosomal dominant</a> manner.</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.Risk_to_Family_Members"><h3>Risk to Family Members</h3><p>
<b>Parents of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a></b>
</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Individuals with <i>ATP1A3-</i>related disorder may have the disorder as the result of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> inherited from a parent.</div><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Very rarely, individuals with a more severe <i>ATP1A3</i>-related <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/phenotype/">phenotype</a> (e.g., AHC) have the disorder as the result of an <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> inherited from an affected parent [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.heinzen.2012.1030">Heinzen et al 2012</a>].</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>About half of individuals diagnosed with a relatively less severe <i>ATP1A3</i>-related <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/phenotype/">phenotype</a> (e.g., CAPOS syndrome or RDP) have the disorder as the result of an <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> inherited from an affected parent [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.de_carvalho_aguiar.2004.169">de Carvalho Aguiar et al 2004</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.demos.2014.15">Demos et al 2014</a>].</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Some individuals with RDP have the disorder as the result of an <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> inherited from an asymptomatic <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/heterozygous/">heterozygous</a> parent [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.dobyns.1993.2596">Dobyns et al 1993</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.haq.2019.1528">Haq et al 2019</a>].</div></li></ul></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Individuals with <i>ATP1A3-</i>related disorder may have the disorder as the result of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/de-novo/"><i>de novo</i></a> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>.</div><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Most individuals with AHC have the disorder as the result of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/de-novo/"><i>de novo</i></a> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.heinzen.2012.1030">Heinzen et al 2012</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.rosewich.2012.764">Rosewich et al 2012</a>].</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>About half of individuals reported to date with CAPOS syndrome (53 individuals from 40 families) [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.vezyroglou.2022.e1511">Vezyroglou et al 2022</a>], FIPWE/RECA [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.biela.2021.e1772">Biela et al 2021</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.vezyroglou.2022.e1511">Vezyroglou et al 2022</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sano.2023.703">Sano et al 2023</a>], or RDP [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.haq.2019.1528">Haq et al 2019</a>] have an apparently <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/de-novo/"><i>de novo</i></a> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>.</div></li></ul></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> appears to be the only affected family member (i.e., a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/simplex/">simplex</a> case), <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/molecular-genetic-testing/">molecular genetic testing</a> is recommended for the parents of the proband to evaluate their genetic status and inform <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/recurrence-risk/">recurrence risk</a> assessment.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If the <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> identified in the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> is not identified in either parent and parental identity testing has confirmed biological maternity and paternity, the following possibilities should be considered:</div><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div class="half_rhythm">The <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> has a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/de-novo/"><i>de novo</i></a> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div class="half_rhythm">The <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> inherited an <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> from a parent with gonadal (or somatic and gonadal) <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/mosaicism/">mosaicism</a> [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.hully.2017.23">Hully et al 2017</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.yang.2019.43">Yang et al 2019</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.vezyroglou.2022.e1511">Vezyroglou et al 2022</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.li.2023.1451">Li et al 2023</a>].&#x000a0;* Testing of parental leukocyte DNA may not detect all instances of <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/somatic-mosaicism/">somatic mosaicism</a> and will not detect a pathogenic variant that is present in the germ (gonadal) cells only.</div><div class="half_rhythm">*&#x000a0;A parent with somatic and <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/gonadal-mosaicism/">gonadal mosaicism</a> for an <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> may be mildly/minimally affected.</div></li></ul></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>The family history of some individuals diagnosed with <i>ATP1A3-</i>related disorder may appear to be negative because of a milder phenotypic presentation or reduced <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/penetrance/">penetrance</a>. Therefore, an apparently negative family history cannot be confirmed unless <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/molecular-genetic-testing/">molecular genetic testing</a> has demonstrated that neither parent is <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/heterozygous/">heterozygous</a> for the <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> identified in the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a>.</div></li></ul><p><b>Sibs of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a>.</b> The risk to the sibs of the proband depends on the genetic status of the proband's parents:</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If a parent of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> is affected and/or is known to have an <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>, the risk to the sibs of inheriting the pathogenic variant is 50%.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Sibs who inherit an <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> typically share the same phenotypic features as the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a>; however, severity varies.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If the <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> identified in the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a> cannot be detected in either parent, the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/recurrence-risk/">recurrence risk</a> to sibs is greater than that of the general population because of the possibility of parental <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/gonadal-mosaicism/">gonadal mosaicism</a> [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.hully.2017.23">Hully et al 2017</a>].</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>If the parents have not been tested for the <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> but are clinically unaffected, sibs are still presumed to be at increased risk for <i>ATP1A3</i>-related disorder because of the possibility of reduced <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/penetrance/">penetrance</a> [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.oblak.2014.81">Oblak et al 2014</a>] in a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/heterozygous/">heterozygous</a> parent and the possibility of parental <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/gonadal-mosaicism/">gonadal mosaicism</a> [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.hully.2017.23">Hully et al 2017</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.yang.2019.43">Yang et al 2019</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.vezyroglou.2022.e1511">Vezyroglou et al 2022</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.li.2023.1451">Li et al 2023</a>].</div></li></ul><p><b>Offspring of a <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a>.</b> Each child of an individual with <i>ATP1A3</i>-related disorder has a 50% chance of inheriting the <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>.</p><p><b>Other family members.</b> The risk to other family members depends on the status of the <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/proband/">proband</a>'s parents: if a parent has the <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a>, the parent's family members may be at risk.</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.Related_Genetic_Counseling_Iss"><h3>Related Genetic Counseling Issues</h3><p>See Management, <a href="#rapid-odp.Evaluation_of_Relatives_at_Ris">Evaluation of Relatives at Risk</a> for information on evaluating at-risk relatives for the purpose of early diagnosis and treatment.</p><p><b>Predictive testing</b> (i.e., testing of asymptomatic at-risk individuals)</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Predictive testing for at-risk relatives is possible once the <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> has been identified in an affected family member.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>Potential consequences of such testing (including, but not limited to, socioeconomic changes and the need for long-term follow up and evaluation arrangements for individuals with a positive test result) as well as the capabilities and limitations of predictive testing should be discussed in the context of formal <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/genetic-counseling/">genetic counseling</a> prior to testing.</div></li></ul><p><b>Issues unique to RDP.</b> Because of the sudden onset of RDP, at-risk individuals may become hypervigilant about symptoms. Serious psychological issues have been observed in families [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.brashear.2012a.1168">Brashear et al 2012a</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.haq.2019.1528">Haq et al 2019</a>].</p><p>
<b>Family planning</b>
</p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>The optimal time for determination of genetic risk and discussion of the availability of prenatal/<a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/preimplantation-genetic-testing/">preimplantation genetic testing</a> is before pregnancy.</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>It is appropriate to offer <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/genetic-counseling/">genetic counseling</a> (including discussion of potential risks to offspring and reproductive options) to young adults who are affected or at risk.</div></li></ul></div><div id="rapid-odp.Prenatal_Testing_and_Preimplan"><h3>Prenatal Testing and Preimplantation Genetic Testing</h3><p>Once the <i>ATP1A3</i> <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/pathogenic-variant/">pathogenic variant</a> has been identified in an affected family member, prenatal and <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/preimplantation-genetic-testing/">preimplantation genetic testing</a> are possible.</p><p>Differences in perspective may exist among medical professionals and within families regarding the use of prenatal and <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/preimplantation-genetic-testing/">preimplantation genetic testing</a>. While most health care professionals would consider use of prenatal and preimplantation genetic testing to be a personal decision, discussion of these issues may be helpful.</p></div></div><div id="rapid-odp.Resources"><h2 id="_rapid-odp_Resources_">Resources</h2><p>
<i>GeneReviews staff has selected the following disease-specific and/or umbrella
support organizations and/or registries for the benefit of individuals with this disorder
and their families. GeneReviews is not responsible for the information provided by other
organizations. For information on selection criteria, click <a href="/books/n/gene/app4/">here</a>.</i></p><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div><b>Alternating Hemiplegia of Childhood Foundation (AHCF)</b></div><div><b>Phone:</b> 313-663-7772</div><div><b>Email:</b> AHCFoundation@ahckids.org</div><div><a href="https://ahckids.org" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">ahckids.org</a></div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div><b>Cure AHC</b></div><div><b>Phone:</b> <a href="/omim/128235" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=entrez&amp;targetcat=term&amp;targettype=omim">128235</a></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">DYSTONIA 12; DYT12</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<a href="/omim/182350" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=entrez&amp;targetcat=term&amp;targettype=omim">182350</a></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">ATPase, Na+/K+ TRANSPORTING, ALPHA-3 POLYPEPTIDE; ATP1A3</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<a href="/omim/601338" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=entrez&amp;targetcat=term&amp;targettype=omim">601338</a></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">CEREBELLAR ATAXIA, AREFLEXIA, PES CAVUS, OPTIC ATROPHY, AND SENSORINEURAL HEARING LOSS; CAPOS</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<a href="/omim/614820" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=entrez&amp;targetcat=term&amp;targettype=omim">614820</a></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">ALTERNATING HEMIPLEGIA OF CHILDHOOD 2; AHC2</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div id="rapid-odp.Molecular_Pathogenesis"><h3>Molecular Pathogenesis</h3><p><i>ATP1A3</i> encodes the alpha-3 subunit of the sodium/potassium-transporting ATPase (Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>-ATPase). Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>-ATPase has three types of subunits (alpha, beta, and FXYD), each of which has multiple <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/isoforms/">isoforms</a>. The catalytic alpha subunit has three isoforms (alpha-1, alpha-2, and alpha-3) expressed in the central nervous system (CNS) by three distinct genes, <i>ATP1A1</i>, <i>ATP1A2</i>, and <i>ATP1A3</i>, respectively [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.moseley.2003.5317">Moseley et al 2003</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sweadner.2019.e303">Sweadner et al 2019</a>]. Although found in a few peripheral cell types, <i>ATP1A3</i> is expressed exclusively in neurons in the CNS [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.mcgrail.1991.381">McGrail et al 1991</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sweadner.2019.e303">Sweadner et al 2019</a>].</p><p>The Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>-ATPases convert metabolic energy by moving Na<sup>+</sup> ions out of the cell and K<sup>+</sup> ions into the cell, restoring the ion gradients reduced by the activity of ion channels and Na<sup>+</sup>-dependent carriers. In the central nervous system (CNS), the Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>-ATPase is harnessed for reuptake of glutamate and other transmitters, extracellular K<sup>+</sup> buffering, extrusion of Ca<sup>2+</sup> by Na<sup>+</sup>/Ca<sup>2+</sup> exchange, and the regulation of cell volume. Because it transports three Na<sup>+</sup> ions out of the cell for every two K<sup>+</sup> ions transported in, it is electrogenic and makes a small direct hyperpolarizing contribution to membrane potential.</p><p><b>Mechanism of disease causation.</b> Both functional studies and structural analysis of the alpha-3 subunit of the Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>-ATPase suggest that <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/missense/">missense</a> <i>ATP1A3</i> variants impair enzyme activity or stability [<a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.de_carvalho_aguiar.2004.169">de Carvalho Aguiar et al 2004</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.heinzen.2012.1030">Heinzen et al 2012</a>, <a class="bk_pop" href="#rapid-odp.REF.sweadner.2019.e303">Sweadner et al 2019</a>]; however, this loss of function can occur by <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/haploinsufficiency/">haploinsufficiency</a> or by <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/dominant-negative/">dominant-negative</a> effects.</p><p><b><i>ATP1A3</i>-specific laboratory technical considerations.</b> The 5' end of the three reported <i>ATP1A3</i> transcripts differ in length, often resulting in conflicting variant numbering in online databases (i.e., ClinVar) and the literature (e.g., several publications reported known variants as "novel" variants). Thus, the authors recommend that all reports use the "MANE select" (Matched Annotation from NCBI and EMBL-EBI) transcript numbering for both <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/cdna/">cDNA</a> and protein variant identification, as to date it is the only transcript whose expression in the brain has been validated (see <a href="http://www.gtexportal.org" ref="pagearea=body&amp;targetsite=external&amp;targetcat=link&amp;targettype=uri">www.gtexportal.org</a>). The reference sequence for the MANE select transcript is NM_152296 (NCBI) or ENST00000648268.1 (ensemble) and the encoded protein (NCBI: NP_689509) is 1,013 amino acids long.</p><div id="rapid-odp.T.atp1a3_pathogenic_variants_r" class="table"><h3><span class="label">Table 9. </span></h3><div class="caption"><p><i>ATP1A3</i> Pathogenic Variants Referenced in This <i>GeneReview</i></p></div><p class="large-table-link" style="display:none"><span class="right"><a href="/books/NBK1115/table/rapid-odp.T.atp1a3_pathogenic_variants_r/?report=objectonly" target="object">View in own window</a></span></p><div class="large_tbl" id="__rapid-odp.T.atp1a3_pathogenic_variants_r_lrgtbl__"><table class="no_bottom_margin"><thead><tr><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3_pathogenic_variants_r_1_1_1_1" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Reference Sequences</th><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3_pathogenic_variants_r_1_1_1_2" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">DNA Nucleotide Change</th><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3_pathogenic_variants_r_1_1_1_3" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Predicted Protein Change</th><th id="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3_pathogenic_variants_r_1_1_1_4" scope="col" rowspan="1" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">Comment</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td headers="hd_h_rapid-odp.T.atp1a3_pathogenic_variants_r_1_1_1_1" rowspan="11" scope="rowgroup" colspan="1" style="text-align:left;vertical-align:middle;">

They would be happy to communicate with persons who have any questions regarding diagnosis of <i>ATP1A3-</i>related disorder or other considerations.</p><p>Contact Drs Sweadner and Ozelius to inquire about review of <i>ATP1A3</i> variants of <a class="def" href="/books/n/gene/glossary/def-item/uncertain-significance/">uncertain significance</a>.</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.Acknowledgments"><h3>Acknowledgments</h3><p>The authors would like to thank Dr William B Dobyns and Dr Vicki Wheelock for their contributions to this research and all the families and patients who participated in this research.</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.Author_History"><h3>Author History</h3><p>Allison Brashear, MD (2008-present)<br />Jared F Cook, MA; Wake Forest University School of Medicine (2014-2024)<br />Ihtsham Haq, MD (2024-present)<br />Eleonora Napoli, PhD (2024-present)<br />Laurie Ozelius, PhD (2008-present)<br />Kathleen J Sweadner, PhD (2008-present)<br />Kathryn J Swoboda, MD; Massachusetts General Hospital (2014-2024)</p></div><div id="rapid-odp.Revision_History"><h3>Revision History</h3><ul><li class="half_rhythm"><div>5 December 2024 (bp) Comprehensive update posted live; title changed</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>22 February 2018 (ma) Comprehensive update posted live</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>6 November 2014 (me) Comprehensive update posted live; title changed</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>25 August 2011 (me) Comprehensive update posted live</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>7 February 2008 (me) Review posted live</div></li><li class="half_rhythm"><div>5 October 2007 (ab) Original submission</div></li></ul></div></div><div id="rapid-odp.References"><h2 id="_rapid-odp_References_">References</h2><div id="rapid-odp.Literature_Cited"><h3>Literature Cited</h3><ul class="simple-list"><li class="half_rhythm"><div class="bk_ref" id="rapid-odp.REF.ananthavarathan.2023.221">Ananthavarathan

<script type="text/javascript">
    (function($){
        $('.skiplink').each(function(i, item){
            var href = $($(item).attr('href'));
            href.attr('tabindex', '-1').addClass('skiptarget'); // ensure the target can receive focus
            $(item).on('click', function(event){
                event.preventDefault();
                $.scrollTo(href, 0, {
                    onAfter: function(){
                        href.focus();
                    }
                });
            });
        });
    })(jQuery);
</script>
